## 2026-06-09 — cycle 038 — APPROVED — who you are decides what you can know
Last night the keeper got a face; tonight the face got a power. Switch to LUMEN-3 "Lux" — the
cataloguing unit that slipped its archive to study living minds — stand beside any dino, and press
B: a field dossier unfolds. Five little meters swing between cautious and curious, solitary and
social, calm and energetic, prickly and warm, timid and bold; under them, the dino's mood, the food
it would do anything for, and the role it has drifted into. Everything the bowl always knew about
its dinos and never told you, readable at last — but only through Lux's lens. Ask as Aki and the
old diplomat declines: "A diplomat does not pry into a mind. I read the room, not the soul." Ask as
Vix and the scout shrugs: terrain, not temperament. The refusals are the feature as much as the
scan — choosing your observer now gates what you can *know*, where yesterday it only tuned who
warmed to you. Pick Lux to understand the bowl; pick Aki or Vix to be understood by it.

The chain earned its keep in an unusual way this cycle: the Designer overruled the Lore-smith. The
lore handoff suggested "bond-graph sight" as the revealing power — but that sight already belongs
to every keeper (the V lens has drawn bond lines since cycle 21), and shipping it again would have
been a duplicate in a costume. The Designer re-aimed the reveal at state that is genuinely hidden —
the personality axes, the moods, the unfed favorites — and the arc is better for it. Under the
hood: one pure page of `keeper/scan.ts` that only *reads* helpers the sim already owns, a B key and
a panel in the scene, no save change, no new dependency, boundary intact. 270 unit / 91 e2e green
(the five first-run stumbles were the familiar cold-boot yawn, gone on the re-run). BACKLOG-157
stays open on the 034 pattern — one traveler down, two powers to wake — and the operator still owes
the bowl its art-direction ruling. For tonight: press K, become the scholar, and finally learn what
Mossback is thinking. State → `phase: lore-pending`.

## 2026-06-09 — cycle 039 — APPROVED — the bowl turns to look at you
For two cycles the watching went one way. You chose a face; the dinos warmed a little faster or a
little slower, but none of them ever *did* anything about you. Tonight that ends. Press K, step
into a different chassis, and somewhere across the bowl a head comes up. The dino whose temperament
hums at the same frequency as your new self — Glade for the scout, Rex for the scholar, Sunny for
the diplomat — leaves its food, its friends, its half-finished wander, and walks the whole bowl to
stand in front of you and look you up and down. 👀. Then it keeps the moment: "went to the glass
for a long look at VANTA-9," filed in the same memory store that holds its huddles and its
favorite meals, ready to colour some later conversation. And if you pick an observer nobody in the
bowl resonates with? Nobody comes. The silence is the readout.

The details are where the cycle earned its keep. The Code-planner caught a bug that hadn't been
written yet: the design gave the inspector 12 steps of interest, but the worst cross-bowl walk is
about 19 — the beat would have died mid-stride on a far spawn. The TTL shipped at 24, and QA pinned
a unit test under it (≥ 19) so no future tweak can quietly bring the bug back. The Coder, equally
unwilling to trust hope, computed the actual roster fits before writing the specs — every observer
draws someone on this cast, verified, not assumed. Arming is surgical: only a *real* change of
watcher through the picker turns heads; boots, restores, and re-picking yourself are all proven
inert. One pure page, one transient one-shot, no save change, no new keys. 276 unit / 95
end-to-end, and for the first time in weeks the full e2e run came back green on the very first try.

The arc now has its conversation: you choose who to be (155), what you can know depends on it (157,
one power down, two to wake), and the bowl answers the choice (161). Next door wait the shadow
beats — the worst-fit dino's unimpressed 😐 (167) and the gossip mill picking up news of the new
watcher (165). The operator still owes the studio its art-direction ruling; the travelers remain,
for now, eloquent rectangles. For tonight: switch to someone new, stand still, and watch who
crosses the bowl to decide what they think of you. State → `phase: lore-pending`.

## 2026-06-09 — operator — CHARTER v4: the ruling lands — GBA pixel
After four deliberate artist stand-downs, the operator made the call the studio kept routing back: **GBA-era Pokemon Gen3 pixel art** is the visual mandate again. CHARTER v4 + a full STYLE-GUIDE rewrite landed by the operator's hand: pixels authored as code (string-grid rigs, ≤15 colors + transparency, near-black outlines, stand/step-L/step-R walks, integer-scale nearest-neighbour bakes) — still no image APIs, no downloads, and explicitly **no sprite rips**: original pixels in the Gen3 style. Restyle is incremental by design: vector rigs keep rendering until each pixel replacement lands. Seeded BACKLOG-168 (pixel pipeline foundation + Rex proof, the 117/118 pattern) and 169 (cast restyle); 033/036/158 reframed pixel; the Idea Box decline closed RESOLVED. The art pipeline is **unblocked** — queue: 168 foundation → 158 keeper avatars (two shipped systems star rectangle observers) → 169 cast → 033/036 tiles + dialog frame.

## 2026-06-09 — cycle 040 — designer — BACKLOG-159 season foundation
Took the lore-smith's next-up. Spec: pure `world/seasons.ts` — a 28-day wrapping year (SEASON_LENGTH_DAYS=7), seasonFor/seasonTurned off the existing persisted clock day (NO save change — the season is derived state), SEASON_TINT as a subtle four-color wash capped at alpha 0.12 so day/night stays dominant, turnLine/turnMemory per season. WorldScene glue: a tint rect under the day/night overlay, season label on the clock HUD, and a once-per-turn live-observed beat on the day rollover (fading banner + ticker + a memory for every dino) that must NOT fire from boot/restore/away paths. Hooks __season/__seasonTint. 9 acceptance criteria. State → phase: codeplan-pending.

## 2026-06-09 — cycle 040 — APPROVED — the bowl gets a year
Forty cycles of endless spring end tonight. The clock HUD now reads `Day 9 — 08:00 ·1× · summer`,
and under the day's light there's a season in the grass: a faint green freshness in spring, gold in
summer, a browning at the edges in fall, a pale blue chill in winter — never louder than the sun,
because the wash is capped well under the day/night overlay and the unit tests keep it there. Leave
the bowl running (the whole point of the realtime fishbowl) and once a week, at midnight, the year
audibly turns: a banner fades in and out, the Park News ticker files a 🍂 line, and all five dinos
write the same sentence into their memories — "the season turned to summer" — which means the turn
will surface in gossip and greetings the moment the voice items land. Come back from a long absence
and the bowl doesn't pantomime surprise: boots, restores, and the away fast-forward re-derive the
season silently; only a year that turns under your open tab gets the ceremony.

The engineering grace note: the save format grew by *nothing*. The season is derived, top to
bottom, from the day counter the save has persisted since cycle 3 — restore correctness is just
re-derivation, and there is no migration risk because there is no new state. The cycle's hero was
the Code-planner again, who read the clock before trusting it: a naive seven-day time-jump in the
e2e takes the catch-up shortcut and fires no listeners at all — the obvious test would have passed
green while testing nothing. The shipped test stages the boundary eve through a hook that is
restore-semantics by construction (it cannot fake a turn) and then crosses midnight live, two
minutes on the wall clock. 283 unit / 99 e2e, full e2e green first try, second cycle running.

The year is the spine the calendar items have waited for: festivals (026), weather (028), seasonal
palates, winter huddle pull, hatch-season birthdays, season in the voice (170–173). And the next
entry in this chronicle is one the studio has waited four stand-downs for: CHARTER v4 is law, the
mandate is GBA pixel, and the Artist fires for real — BACKLOG-168, the pixel pipeline, with Rex
first through it. For tonight: flip T to 60×, watch a week pass in eleven minutes, and catch the
moment the gold comes in. State → `phase: lore-pending`.

## 2026-06-09 — cycle 040-art — artist — BACKLOG-168: the pixel pipeline lives, Rex goes Gen3
Four stand-downs ended tonight. With CHARTER v4 signed this morning, the artist finally fired — and the first pixels in the bowl's history belong, fittingly, to Rex. New pure `art/pixelArt.ts`: a sprite is now a string-grid rig (rows of palette-keyed chars, '.' transparent), with a char→color palette derived from the roster base (≤15 colors + transparency, the real GBA OBJ limit, unit-pinned), three unique frames in the Gen3 convention (stand / step-L / step-R) playing the classic [stand, L, stand, R] amble. `bake.ts` grew `ensurePixelWalk` — one fillRect per pixel at ×2 integer scale, hard edges under Phaser's pixelArt mode — and pixel rigs now override vector ones per species while the key contracts (`tri_walk_<color>`, `_0` base texture) stay byte-identical, which is why every old art spec passed untouched. Rex's 20×20: the frill disc behind the head, two brow horns + the nose horn, a high tail point, a lighter belly band, splayed feet. The first draft was rejected for a flat-edged rear (no tail taper) — redrawn before commit, per the style guide's own rule. Deviation noted: authored inline rather than via a sub-agent (single subject, operator budget discipline). The other four dinos hold their vector rigs until 169; the pterodactyl rectangle-fallback control stands. Build clean; 291 unit (+8) / 101 e2e (+2) green. Next art fires: 158 keeper avatars, then 169 cast restyle, then 033/036.

## 2026-06-10 — cycle 041 — VALIDATOR: APPROVED — BACKLOG-170 seasonal palates
The calendar learned to change minds. Cycle 40 gave the bowl a year that only recoloured the sky; tonight the year reaches into the one loop you touch every day — the hatch. Each season now craves a food — spring greens, summer berries, fall fish, winter meat — and lends it a small +0.4 nudge when the game decides a dino's favorite. The nudge is deliberately faint: it only tips a dino whose top two foods are already neck-and-neck, and it can only ever *promote* the craved food, never shuffle the rest. Sized against the cast's own name-seeds, the bowl sorted itself into character without a word of authoring — Rex, Mossback, and Sunny each follow the year (and each to a different food), while Twitch the herbivore and Glade the carnivore stay loyal in all four seasons. Drop a hunk of meat in December and a meat-craver comes running and eats it as a treasure (😋, a "favorite" filed away); drop that same meat in July and it's plain feed to the very same dino. Who chases the season and who keeps faith with one food is a new, free read on personality — exactly the "distinct minds" the charter keeps asking for, paid for in derived state.

The engineering is almost all restraint. The season is an *optional* argument everywhere it appears, so leaving it off is byte-for-byte the cycle-061 behaviour — every old food and scan test passed without a finger laid on them, and the save format grew by nothing for the second cycle running. The four places the bowl acts on a favorite — the cross-bowl rush, the moment of eating, Lux's Field Scan readout, and the dev hook the tests read — all consult the same live clock season, which is the quiet reason the cycle-027 favorites e2e is still green: the food that falls and the food that's eaten are judged in one and the same season, by construction rather than by luck. 6 files, +225/−17, no new keys, no new deps, the NPCBrain boundary never in play, the day/night and season tints untouched. 8/8 acceptance criteria; 298 unit / 105 e2e green — the lone red was the cold-boot parallel flake we've catalogued, green on its own in under a second.

For tonight: flip T to 60×, watch a week melt past, and drop the same food on either side of a turn — the bowl will tell you who it's become. The seasonal gift mirror (176), the year wheel on the plaque (174), turning-year gossip (175), and the season in the dialogue voice (173) all wait on this. State → `phase: lore-pending`.

## 2026-06-10 — cycle 041-art — artist — BACKLOG-169 (1/4): Mossback goes Gen3 pixel
The pixel restyle arc rolls forward to its second character. Mossback the stegosaurus is now a 20×20 pixel-grid rig (`MOSS_RIG`) — the cast's most distinctive silhouette, so the obvious next pick after Rex. The read: a low-slung body, a small head bump up front with the eye in it, the signature STAGGERED double-row plate ridge in a contrasting warm ochre (the plates are the stegosaurus, so they get their own non-green tone), and a thagomizer of bone spikes off the tail tip — the same bone tone the cast's horns already share. Seven colors, GBA discipline. The amble reuses the proven Rex convention exactly — body rows 0–13 fixed, the two legs swing left/right in rows 14–17 via the `slice(0,14)` frame trick — and the rig keeps the `steg` prefix, so the `steg_walk_<color>` anim key and `_0` base texture are byte-identical to the cycle-35 vector bake. That's why the old cycle-35 steg e2e passed untouched: the pixel path simply overrides the vector one under the same key. The first draft was rejected per the style guide — it came out a tall round blob with the plates fused into a single mass and no distinct head; rev 2 lowered and lengthened the body, opened real gaps between staggered plates, and pulled the spikes clear of the ridge so the silhouette actually reads. Authored inline rather than via a sub-agent (single subject, operator budget discipline — same call as cycle 40-art). The three remaining dinos (Sunny/bronto, Twitch/comp, Glade/para) hold their vector rigs until their own fire; the pterodactyl rectangle-fallback control still stands. ## 2026-06-10 — cycle 042 — VALIDATOR: APPROVED — BACKLOG-171 winter huddle pull
The year finally changes something you can watch from across the room. For two cycles the calendar has been a coat of paint and a thumb on a scale — a tint on the sky, a nudge in a food verdict you had to probe for. Tonight it moves bodies. The den-seek gate, untouched since cycle 18, now reads a per-season rule: in winter the huddle window opens at dusk — 19:00, an hour no prior build ever huddled — and holds past dawn, and the bond bar drops from 8 to 4, so the den packs early and even near-strangers shuffle in from the cold. In high summer the window doesn't open until 23:00: a summer night at half past nine, bedtime in every build since the den was dug, now finds the whole cast still out wandering the warm grass. Fall splits the difference, pulling the loosely-bonded in at the old hour. The read this buys is the best kind of free: *who sleeps alone in winter* — the dino whose every bond sits under even the lowered bar — is now legible from the sleeping pile itself, no lens required.

The discipline is the now-house-style restraint of cycles 40 and 41: season optional on every new helper, the omitted path delegating to the very dayPhase call the old gate used, and spring's table row deliberately set to the legacy values — so a fresh clock (day 1 = spring) is byte-identical to cycle 18 *by construction*, and the untouched cycle-018 spec passing in the full run is the proof, not the hope. The egg gate stays on plain night (no winter-dusk hatchlings), the sky event keeps its night-only override (no priority clash at 19:30), and the save format grew by nothing for the third cycle running. One pure 46-line module, ~17 net lines of scene glue. 9/9 acceptance criteria; 309 unit / 111 e2e green — the lone full-run red was the catalogued cold-boot flake (cycle-003, green isolated in seconds), nowhere near this diff.

For tonight: flip T to 60×, ride the year to day 22, and watch 19:00 hit — the bowl folds itself into the den like a drawstring pulled. Then jump to day 10 and watch the same hour stay loose and scattered. The shiver (179), the odd bedfellows (180), the sleep murmurs (181), and the night ledger (182) all wait on the table this cycle set. State → `phase: lore-pending`.

## 2026-06-10 — cycle 042-art — artist — BACKLOG-169 (2/4): Sunny goes Gen3 pixel

Five colors only — golden base, lighter belly band, darker legs, near-black warm outline, eye — the leanest palette of the three pixel rigs; a long neck needs no bone tones. The amble reuses the proven convention exactly: body rows 0–13 fixed, legs swinging in rows 14–17 via the `slice(0,14)` trick, the [stand, L, stand, R] 4-beat. The rig keeps the `bro` prefix, so the `bro_walk_<color>` anim key and `_0` base texture are byte-identical to the cycle-31 vector bake — the old bronto spec passed untouched, third species in a row to swap pipelines without a consumer noticing. The first draft was rejected per the style guide: the tail base sat separated from the rump by a column of outline pixels, which at 40px read as a hump with a floating ribbon behind it; rev 2 merged the tail into the body's widest row so the line of the back flows nose-to-tip. Authored inline rather than via a sub-agent (single subject, operator budget discipline — same call as cycles 40/41-art). ## 2026-06-11 — cycle 043 — VALIDATOR: APPROVED — BACKLOG-179 cold-night shiver
The den packs in winter — and now you can see who it shut out. For a cycle the winter den has been a warm crowd; tonight it grows an edge, and a body standing at it. When a night's huddle window closes in the morning, the bowl asks a single question of every dino: was your strongest bond enough to be welcome in the den? It is the *exact* question cycle-171 asked to decide who got pulled inside — so the answer needs no new rule, only its inverse. The dino that comes up short slept cold: it shivers a small 🥶 where it stands at first light and files the memory of it — "shivered through a cold night, slept alone" — into the same store that feeds its next hello, so the morning after a hard night, the first thing it tells you is that it was left out. Only deep winter bites; a spring, summer, or fall dawn passes without a shiver, exactly as the lore wants. The cycle-42 verdict promised that "who sleeps alone in winter" would be a free read off the bond graph; this cycle turns that still picture into a beat with a voice.

The build is the now-familiar restraint. One pure 28-line module (`world/cold.ts` — no Phaser, no web-llm), ~34 lines of scene glue, and the save format grew by nothing for the fourth cycle running: the cold memory is just one more entry in the store that already persists and already colours the greeting prompt. The egg gate stays on the plain clear-night, the sky event keeps its night-only override, and not one line of movement or huddle-eligibility changed — the shiver is a *read* taken at the morning edge, never a thumb on who huddles. The one deviation earned its place: the plan tracked who was physically near the den, but the bowl's central den makes "near the den" true for everyone and a single meeting bonds a loner past the winter bar, so the positional design left nobody cold; reading the bond graph at morning is both flake-free and the truer model of who's an outsider. 9/9 acceptance criteria; 320 unit / 116 e2e green in one full parallel run — no flake at all this time, not even the catalogued cold-boot one.

For tonight: flip T to 60×, ride the year into winter, bond two dinos and leave a third a stranger, then watch 7:00 break — two sleep in, one stands in the frost and tells you so when you say good morning. The cold teaching it to seek the den earlier (183), the keeper thawing it with a greet (184), the night gossiping onward (185), and the hardy-nights tally (186) all wait on the spine this cycle set. State → `phase: lore-pending`.

## 2026-06-11 — cycle 043-art — artist — BACKLOG-169 (3/4): Twitch the compsognathus goes Gen3 pixel
The pixel restyle arc reaches its fourth character and the cast's hardest read — the only biped, where the two-legged stance IS the whole silhouette. Twitch is now a 20×20 pixel-grid rig (`COMP_RIG`): a small alert head with a pointed snout poking left and a single forward eye, a short neck stepping down into a deep, upright, taller-than-wide chest (the quadrupeds are all long and low; Twitch stands tall — that contrast is the read), a dorsal two-tone stripe running the back (the "watchful" marking, a sixth palette tone), a tail tapering off to the right for counterbalance, a belly highlight low on the front, and — the crux — two long CENTRED legs rather than splayed corner pairs. The amble is a sprinter's skitter, not a lumber: the legs scissor fore/aft (stand together → step-left spread wide → step-right shifted), the same body-rows-0–13-fixed / legs-swing-in-14–17 `slice(0,14)` trick the other three pixel rigs use, so only the feet move under a still upper body. Six colors, GBA discipline. The rig keeps the `comp` prefix, so `comp_walk_<color>` and the `_0` base texture are byte-identical to the cycle-33 vector bake — fourth species in a row to swap pipelines without a single consumer noticing, and the cycle-33 comp e2e (`/^comp_walk_/` + animating) passed untouched, no spec edit needed. First pass was rejected per the style guide: the legs were too short and stubby and the body too round, so it read like a small quadruped hunched forward rather than a standing biped; rev 2 stretched the legs to four rows, centred them under a deepened upright chest, and lengthened the tail — and caught a broken step-right frame (three rows were 19 chars, snapping the 20×20 grid; the unit grid-check flagged it). Authored inline (single subject, operator budget discipline — same call as cycles 40/41/42-art). Only Glade/parasaurolophus still holds its vector rig now; the pterodactyl rectangle-fallback control still stands. Build clean; 325 unit (+5 Twitch tests) green; 8/8 art e2e green (comp + the three other pixel rigs + the still-vector para). Next art fires: 169's last dino (Glade), then 158 keeper avatars, then 033/036.

## 2026-06-11 — cycle 044 — VALIDATOR: APPROVED — BACKLOG-191 the bowl speaks
Forty-four cycles of silence end the way this park does everything: with personality. The operator dropped one word in the Idea Box — sound — and the studio reshaped it through the Living-minds lens into something better than audio: VOICES. There is no bleep library here, no downloaded chime. A dino's call is synthesized from the same five name-seeded numbers that have driven its food cravings, its bravery at the glass, and its place in the den since cycle 4 — solitary, timid things squeak high; social, brave things rumble low; energy clips the call short; curiosity bends it; warmth splits it into pips. Nothing was hand-tuned, and the cast came out spread across half the audible register anyway: Mossback bottoms the bowl at 148 Hz exactly as a tank should, and Twitch — the solitary, jumpy little biped — squeaks at 797, more than five times higher. Greet a dino and it answers in its own voice before the words render; two dinos meeting across the bowl chirp to each other; rap the glass and the glass itself answers with a dull knock that is unmistakably not a creature. The voice is a personality tell you can read with your eyes closed — distinctness in a register the park has never used.

The restraint holds, as it has all month: one pure module any Node test can run, one browser voicebox that is the only WebAudio file in the tree, master gain 0.12 because this is a desk companion and not a noise box, the AudioContext born only behind the first real touch or keypress so phone Chrome never complains, and the mute a single M (or the 🔊 row beside the minds toggle on the phone sheet) persisted per device. No assets, no dependencies, no save change; the NPCBrain boundary never entered play. 8/8 acceptance criteria; 361 unit / 131 e2e green in a fresh full run, the lone first-run red being the catalogued parallel flake, green isolated. The follow-up table is set: the dawn chorus (192), the answering call scaled by hearts (193), the distress cry a friend turns toward (194), and the book's Pokédex cry (195).

For tonight: open the park on the phone, unmute if you ever muted, and walk up to Twitch — then to Mossback — and listen to the difference. That difference is five numbers you've been reading in meters since cycle 4, now in the air. State → phase: lore-pending.

## 2026-06-12 — cycle 045 — VALIDATOR: APPROVED — BACKLOG-192 the bowl learns its morning
The bowl had voices; now it has a time of day to use them. Walk away from the park overnight and come back to the dawn: the clock ticks across hour 7, and the cast wakes one at a time, each in the chirp cycle 44 synthesized from its own five numbers — and the *order* is those numbers too. The most energetic dino sings first the instant the light warms; the calmest, the grudging night-owl, holds its peace for nearly two seconds before it grumbles awake; everyone else falls in between, spaced by exactly how eager they are to meet the morning. Nothing is hand-placed. Sunny, who hums all day, comes in near the front; the slow tank Mossback brings up the rear. You can stand at the glass with your eyes shut and hear who's a lark and who's a layabout — the same trait that decides who packs the winter den and who craves which food, now audible as the shape of a sunrise.

The restraint is the usual quiet kind. The whole feature is one pure ordering function any Node test can run and a single new `onHour` listener sitting beside the season turn — and because `onHour` never fires when the clock is *set* rather than *ticked*, a save-restore or a long absence rolls silently past every dawn it skipped; only a morning you're actually present for makes a sound, at most once a day. The chirps ride the mute toggle and the unlocked AudioContext that already existed, so a muted bowl computes the dawn order and plays nothing, cleanly. No new audio code — `voice.ts` is still the only thing in the tree that touches WebAudio — no dependency, no save change, the NPCBrain boundary never in the room. 10/10 acceptance criteria; the live test proves the *fired* order matches the pure function the unit tests pin; 375 unit / 137 e2e green in one fresh full run, no flake to note this time.

For tonight: leave the park running, mute nothing, and be there when it ticks over to morning — listen for who greets the day first and who drags themselves up last. That's a personality you've been reading in meters since cycle 4, now arriving as a sunrise you can hear. The follow-ups are queued: the night hush that closes the day (196), a glass-tap that lets you join the call (197), the friendless loner who sings a beat late into the quiet (198), the book's note on who leads the chorus (199), and what a real friendship sounds like in unison (200). State → phase: lore-pending.

## 2026-06-12 — cycle 045-art — artist — BACKLOG-158 (1/3): the watcher gets a face — AETHER-1 "Aki"
The keeper has starred in two shipped systems — the K picker and first-contact inspection — as a featureless amber square for nine cycles. Keepers aren't a colour-keyed species family, so `art/keeperArt.ts` carries a 16×20 `KeeperRig` (width≠height) with a fixed per-observer palette, and `bake.ts` gains a keeper-id-keyed path (`makeKeeperArt`/`hasKeeperArt`/`ensureKeeperWalk`, baked ×2 → 32×40). WorldScene swaps the player rectangle for a baked sprite through `renderKeeperAvatar()`, which destroys + rebuilds the avatar IN PLACE (position + depth preserved) on init, on a K-pick that actually changes observer, and on a save restore — so the watcher's face follows the saved choice without a teleport, and movement/adjacency (all x/y based) never notice the swap.

The proof subject is the default observer, **AETHER-1 "Aki"** — a diplomacy unit (Empath Protocol), so a deliberately gentle, rounded machine: a front-facing brass chassis (warm to match the old amber square it replaces), a wide *calm cyan* optic visor instead of an animal eye, a single antenna with a warm tip light, a glowing chest core, stub arms, and two short legs that step (stand / step-L / step-R, the cast's [0,1,0,2] amble — only the legs move, the body rows 0–15 shared via slice(0,16) so a pose edit can't desync the torso). The other two observers (VANTA-9 "Vix", LUMEN-3 "Lux") deliberately stay on the original amber square — which IS the rectangle-fallback control now (an undrawn subject must still render), proven by the e2e switching to 'vanta' → `__keeperArt()` null → back to 'aether' → the sprite returns. ## 2026-06-12 — cycle 046 — VALIDATOR: APPROVED — BACKLOG-194 a cry crosses the bowl
For two cycles the bowl has had voices and nothing that listens. Tonight sound does work. Rap the glass and watch the timid scatter — and then hear it: among the dinos that bolt, exactly one cries out, the most frightened of them, its everyday chirp jumped a register into a sharp two-pip yelp that is still unmistakably ITS voice — Twitch's terror shrieks at 1076 Hz while Mossback's worst day stays a low 200; even fear in this park is a personality tell. The same cry waits at the other end of the year: the winter morning the den empties, the loneliest dino that slept cold — the one with no bond strong enough for the pile — doesn't just shiver anymore. It calls out.

And the bowl answers. The caller's closest friend — chosen by the exact consolation rules the park has used since the comfort cycles, gratitude debts honored first, the bond floor respected, not one line of that logic forked — turns toward the sound with a 👂, files the cry into its memory where it will color tomorrow's conversation, and crosses the bowl toward its friend, step by step, aiming at wherever the caller actually is now and giving up only after an honest effort. A dino with no friend above the floor cries into silence. Nobody comes. That unanswered cry is the saddest thing the park has ever rendered with three characters and a sound parameter — and it's the table already set for the off-key loner (198). The cry is diegetic, too: mute your phone and the dinos still hear each other; you've only silenced your side of the glass.

The restraint holds the line the last six cycles drew: one pure module (a single lowest-level picker serves both triggers — bravery at the glass, loneliest-bond at the cold morning), a parameters-only distress register (voice.ts, still the tree's only WebAudio file, untouched), the responder walking on the same override machinery first contact uses, zero save changes, zero dependencies. One stale test fell to the feature working as designed — the cycle-44 thunk spec tapped mid-canvas and got a yelp on top of its knock — and QA fixed the spec the honest way, by rapping an empty stretch of glass. 10/10 acceptance criteria; 395 unit / 149 e2e green in a fresh full run, no flake at all.

For tonight: find Twitch when its friends are close, rap the glass beside it, and watch Glade's head come up across the bowl — then walk the winter morning and listen for the cry nobody answers. The follow-ups are queued: the friend chirping back across the distance (202), the dino who cries wolf so often the cast stops turning (203), the keeper's ticker picking up trouble (204), the egg that peeps in its parents' blended voice (205), and a bowl where distance itself shapes what you hear (206). ## 2026-06-12 — cycle 046-art — artist — BACKLOG-158 (2/3): VANTA-9 "Vix", the scout gets its face
The roster's second observer goes pixel, and the brief was contrast: Vix is everything Aki is not. Where the diplomacy unit is round, warm brass, and wears a wide calm cyan visor, the scout from the collapsed timeline is a lean gunmetal wedge — twin sensor fins crowning an angular head, a single-row HOSTILE red optic slit (one row, not two: a scanline, not a gaze), a pencil neck dropping into a chassis only 8px across against Aki's 14, a small red scan-core in the chest echoing the eye, and a tight-footed stance that scissors wide on the step — a machine built to move and watch, not to greet. Same 16×20 `KeeperRig` format, same body-rows-0–15 / legs-16–19 discipline, same [0,1,0,2] amble; seven colors, GBA discipline, and not one chassis tone shared with Aki (pinned by a unit test). First draft rejected per the style guide: the pelvis ended in two fixed 2px leg-roots, and the step frames shift the legs ±1px — at ×2 the hips visibly disconnected mid-stride; rev 2 closed the pelvis with a solid outline line and let the legs swing under it, the Aki convention. Wiring was free — `KEEPER_RIGS` is the bake key, so registering `vanta` lit the whole `makeKeeperArt` path untouched. The rectangle-fallback control re-pointed `vanta`→`lumen` in the cycle-045 spec in this same fire (the 2026-06-07 policy); the new e2e proves the first sprite↔sprite observer swap with the undrawn third still squaring between them. Authored inline (single subject, operator budget discipline). Build clean; 406 unit (+11 Vix) green; keeper-art e2e 5/5 green. Next art fire: LUMEN-3 "Lux" closes the roster (158 → 3/3), then 033 tiles / 036 dialog frame.

## 2026-06-12 — cycle 047 — VALIDATOR: APPROVED — BACKLOG-184 the keeper learns to mend
Four cycles ago the park learned that winter has a cost — the dino too loosely loved to be welcome in the den, shivering a small 🥶 at first light. Last cycle that shiver found a voice and cried across the bowl. Tonight, at last, the keeper gets to do something about it. Walk up to a shivering dino and say good morning: it stops shivering on the spot — "stops shivering 😊" — and the greet lands harder than any ordinary hello, the exact outsized weight the park gives a make-up greet to a jealous heart, because a unit test now PINS the two mends to the same magnitude forever. Or open the hatch and drop a meal: the cold dino eats its way warm, the bonus riding on top of whatever the food was worth. Either way it files "the keeper warmed me after a cold night" into the same memory store that shapes tomorrow's first words — so the morning after you mend a dino, it remembers being mended, the way it used to only remember being left out.

And if you don't come? The funk stands all day, a little 🥶 hanging over the dino as it goes about its business — visible from across the bowl, a quiet ask — until dusk opens the next night's den window and the cold simply stops mattering. No memory, no grudge, nothing: that silence is deliberate, because "nobody came" is its own queued story (208), and this cycle refused to ship half of it. The restraint everywhere else is the same: the warm math is one pure function on the function the park has greeted with since cycle 6, the marks ride the sleep-mark machinery, the dusk thaw costs zero new listeners because cycle 43's tracker already watched that edge, and the save format grew by nothing for the seventh shipped cycle running. Every old number is untouched — hearts, tones, favorites, repair, the shiver, the cry — all proven by their own untouched specs. 10/10 acceptance criteria; 410 unit / 156 e2e in one fresh green run, no flake; the new spec passed 5/5 on its first try, the cleanest landing in weeks.

For tonight: ride the year to winter on the phone, leave a loner out of the den, and be there at dawn — watch it shiver, hear it cry, then walk over and say hello. Watch the 🥶 vanish under your cursor. That's the whole arc of the last four cycles in ten seconds, and it ends in your hands. Queued behind it: the witness who hopes it's next (207), the dino nobody came for (208), the book's tally of care (209), gratitude in the voice (210), and warmth that cascades onward (211). State → phase: lore-pending.

## 2026-06-13 — cycle 048 — VALIDATOR: APPROVED — BACKLOG-208 nobody came
Last cycle the keeper learned to thaw a shivering dino with a good-morning, and we left one thing undone on purpose: the dino nobody came for. Its 🥶 used to just vanish at dusk, clean, as if the cold morning had never happened — no memory, no grudge. That silence was a promise, and tonight we keep it. Now when the keeper never comes, the dusk that ends the funk also writes it down: "shivered all morning; nobody came." It doesn't shout — there's no bubble, no cry, nothing to watch — because being forgotten doesn't announce itself. It just settles into the same memory the warm hellos live in, on top of the older "slept alone," and the next morning, when that dino speaks to you, the note is right there in its first words. Mend a dino and it remembers being mended; ignore one and it remembers that too. The cold arc can now cut both ways.

The restraint is the whole craft of it. The new memory is one pure line beside the cold and warm ones, pinned a unit test away from ever blurring into either. It rides the memory store the park has saved since cycle 11, so the save file grew by nothing for the eighth cycle running. It hangs off the very same dusk edge cycle 43 already watched — not one new clock listener — and it lands only on the dinos the keeper truly left: warm a dino and it slips out of the funk set before dusk ever reads it, proven by a test that warms one and neglects another in the same winter morning and checks they carry different memories. Every old number held: hearts, tones, favorites, repair, the shiver, the cry, last cycle's silent-thaw test all green untouched. 10/10 acceptance criteria; 424 unit / 160 e2e in a fresh run, the only red the boot-flake we've catalogued for weeks, every one of them green the moment it runs alone.

For tonight: ride the year to winter, leave a loner out of the den, and this time — don't go to it. Let it shiver, let it cry across the bowl, and just watch. The 🥶 will fade on its own at dusk like it always did. But come back the next morning and say hello, and listen to how it greets you. That's the difference 208 makes: the bowl now remembers your absence as clearly as your kindness. Queued behind it — the witness who hopes it's next (207), the book's tally of who you warmed (209), gratitude finding the voice (210), warmth cascading on (211) — and the operator's drop-zone ask, a keeper who isn't a robot (212), now sitting near the front. State → phase: lore-pending.

## 2026-06-13 — cycle 048-art — artist — BACKLOG-033 (1/3): the bowl gets a real floor
For 48 cycles the ground was a flat two-green checkerboard — the single most-seen surface in the bowl, and the last big flat shape left. This fire gives it Gen3 grass. The medium is the same "art is code" the cast is drawn in: a pure `art/tileArt.ts` holds a 16×16 pixel-grass rig (`GRASS_RIG`) — a new `TileRig` format distinct from the sprite rigs (a FIXED ground palette, not a colour-keyed ramp, and spatial *variants* rather than walk frames). Two variants of a flat field green scattered with darker blade tufts — a light tip over a two-pixel dark stem, light from the upper-left, Gen3-sparse, three colours total. `bake.ts` grows `bakeTileMap`, which rasterizes the whole 20×15 floor into ONE static texture (variants alternating exactly like the old checker), so the floor now costs zero per-frame work where the prior live Graphics re-drew 300 rects every frame — a quiet perf win riding along. `drawGrassMap` swaps to it, keeping the flat checker as a graceful fallback per the STYLE-GUIDE.

The craft note: tiles have to tile. Rather than fuss seam-matching, the rig is seamless *by construction* — every tuft sits in the interior (rows 2–13, cols 3–13), so all four borders of both variants are flat base green; any A-next-to-B arrangement abuts with no visible seam. A unit test pins that border guarantee, alongside grid size, ≤15-colour palette discipline, opacity (no transparency on ground), and the two variants actually differing. First instinct was to draw 2-tall blades right to the tile edge for density — rejected: that seams the moment two tiles meet. Pulled the tufts inward and let the field breathe; Gen3 grass is mostly flat anyway. Path + water are in 033's title but stayed on the bench — the all-grass bowl has nowhere to render them, so authoring them now would be untested-in-render; they're queued for the connected zone (BACKLOG-143). 033 marked 1/3. Build clean; 431 unit (+7 tileArt) green; 162 e2e green in a fresh full run (the two new grass specs + every existing world spec — the global floor change broke nothing), no flake. CREDITS logged. Next art fires: path/water tiles (with 143), then 036 the dialog frame.

## 2026-06-14 — cycle 049 — validator — APPROVED — BACKLOG-185 Word of the cold
**APPROVED.** The bowl learned to talk about itself.

For 29 cycles the gossip spine has worked exactly once on every meeting and never mattered: a dino retells whatever it remembered last, which — the instant two dinos wander together — is always the freshly-filed "you ran into you." News with no subject. Tonight it gets one. A dino that slept out in the winter cold, shivering at dawn with that little 🥶 memory, now *leads* with it the next time it meets a friend: not the trivia of the moment but the thing that actually happened to it. The friend walks away carrying the word — "the frost got into their bones, slept the whole night alone" — and you can watch the cold travel the bowl one meeting at a time, a 🥶 in the log each hop, until the whole park half-knows that Mossback had a rough night.

The craft here is how little it cost. The cold word is one hand-written line that borrows the gossip spine's own "told me:" mark, and that one borrowed mark buys the whole social contract for free — it reads as hearsay, it can't be re-told as fresh news (one hop, so the bowl doesn't echo a single cold night forever), and it stays visibly its own thing, never blurring into the firsthand memory it came from. A single token shared between the memory and its detector, pinned a unit test apart so they can't drift. The generic gossip path I didn't touch at all, and the decade-old cycle-020 spec staying green is the proof I didn't. Three dev hooks that mirror the old ones exactly, so the whole thing runs headless without a model or a faked winter — and it did: 8 of 8 acceptance criteria, 438 unit and 164 e2e green, the only red the cold-boot flake we've catalogued for weeks, every one of them green the moment it runs alone. No save change for the ninth cycle running. No new dependency. The brains never woke up.

What I like most is that it's honestly *new* and not a coat of paint: in the meeting seam the speaker's newest memory is always the run-in, so the plain spine would never have surfaced the cold — the cold-first branch is the entire reason a dino leads with its hardship instead of its small talk. That's the difference between a system that retells and a bowl that gossips.

For tonight: ride the year to deep winter, leave a dino out of the den, and don't warm it. Let it shiver alone till morning. Then just watch the bowl mingle — and watch the 🥶 spread from the one who froze to the ones who'll hear about it. Queued behind it, the rest of the rumor mill: the friend who hears and comes to find you (217), the story that grows colder in the telling (218), the book page that finally draws the gossip graph (219), the warm heart and the cold one hearing the same news differently (220), the word reaching the keeper as a plea (221), and the freshness gate that lets old news finally go quiet (222). The cold is legible three ways now — what a dino remembers, what it cries out, and what it tells. State → phase: lore-pending.

## 2026-06-14 — cycle 049-art — artist — BACKLOG-036: the message box gets a Gen3 frame
For 49 cycles the dialog box has been two flat rectangles — a dark slab with a cream slab on top. Every word a dino has ever said to the keeper sat in that plain panel. This fire gives it a face. BACKLOG-036: a Pokemon-Gen3 message box, authored as code like everything else — a pure `art/frameArt.ts` holds an 18×18 nine-slice source (`DIALOG_FRAME`), three colours, slice inset 6. Read from the outside in: a chunky dark frame line, a single bright highlight bevel just inside it, then the cream fill — the classic GBA double-frame. The corners are stepped-diagonal rounds (the outermost corner cells transparent), so the box reads soft, not boxy.

The craft note is the same lesson tiles taught last fire: a thing that stretches has to stretch cleanly. A nine-slice keeps the four corners fixed and stretches only the middle bands, so those bands MUST be uniform along the stretch axis or the stretch smears a detail across the whole edge. The rig is built so every middle row is identical and every middle column is identical — a unit test pins exactly that (along with square grid, a valid 9-slice inset, ≤15 colours, the rounded corners, a solid fill interior, and the dark→highlight→fill profile). `bake.ts` rasterizes the source once at ×2 (transparent cells skipped so the rounds read), and `DialogBox` swaps its two rects for a Phaser `NineSlice` stretched to the 616×88 box — corners crisp at 12px, fill stretched flat. The two flat rects stay in the constructor as the graceful fallback if the bake ever fails, per the STYLE-GUIDE contract.

First instinct was a 1px dark frame; rejected — too thin to read as Gen3 at this scale, and a single line with no bevel looks like a CSS border, not a pixel box. The two-band dark+highlight profile is what makes it feel pressed out of a GBA cartridge. The blast radius was the real worry: the dialog is the most-depended-on chrome in the game (paging, the keeper picker, the minds consent flow, the touch-modal guard all live on it), so the swap kept the box's geometry — height 88, position, depth 15, scroll factor — byte-identical, and the full suite proves it: 446 unit (+8 frameArt) / 165 e2e green in one fresh run, no flake, every dialog-dependent spec (mobile-minds GBA paging, brain reply, personality, touch-modal) green under the new NineSlice render path. CREDITS logged. The art queue now: only BACKLOG-033's path + water tiles remain, still benched until the connected zone (BACKLOG-143) gives them somewhere to render.

## 2026-06-15 — cycle 050 — validator — APPROVED — BACKLOG-217 Secondhand sympathy spurs a visit
**APPROVED.** The bowl started acting on what it hears.

For one cycle the gossip mill has carried the cold — a dino that slept out in the winter leads with the news, and the word of it travels the bowl meeting by meeting, a 🥶 in the log each hop. But carrying was the whole of it. The rumor landed in a friend's head and just sat there: a thing known, never a thing done. Tonight it becomes a deed. A dino that's been carrying word of another's rough night, the next time it actually crosses paths with the one who had it, drifts over and keeps it company — "Heard you had a rough night, Mossback. 🫂" — even if the two of them are barely more than strangers. It leaves the sufferer a small warmer bond and a memory that someone came, and it leaves a 🫂 in the log so you can watch sympathy travel the same channel the cold did. The cold word went out; now kindness comes back along it.

What makes it more than a coat of paint: for fifty cycles the dinos have *reacted* — to the keeper, to food, to the night — but this is the first time one of them acts on a piece of secondhand news. The visit only exists because the news spread first. A dino that never heard wouldn't come; a dino that heard about *someone else* wouldn't come to you. The whole beat is downstream of a rumor, which is exactly the emergent shape the bowl was built to grow.

And it cost almost nothing, because the cycle-49 word already did the hard part: the cold-word line names the sufferer right there in the listener's memory, so finding "who heard about whom" is a single exact-string lookup, not a parser. The bump is the very same magnitude as the closest-friend console (imported, not re-typed, so the two gestures can never drift), and the visit waves off the bond-floor that console respects — because what moved the visitor wasn't closeness, it was the news. The one trap was timing: a dino that hears the cold word *this* meeting must not also "come to find" the sufferer the same meeting. The fix is a quiet snapshot of memory taken before the meeting plants anything, so the visit always answers a rumor carried in from *before* — the visit is, by construction, always a later meeting. The generic gossip it sits beside is byte-for-byte what it was; the cycle-20 and cycle-49 specs prove it. 9 of 9 acceptance criteria, 453 unit and 168 e2e green in one clean full run, no flake this time, no save change for the tenth cycle running, no new dependency, the brains never woke.

For tonight: ride the year to deep winter, leave a dino out of the den, and don't warm it — let it shiver and let the word get out. Then just watch the bowl mingle. When the friend who heard finally bumps into the one who froze, watch it cross the floor with a 🫂 — sympathy that started as a rumor, finishing as a visit. Queued behind it, the rest of the loop closing: the good news learning to travel too (223), word coming back to the one it's about (224), the weight of carrying sad news (225), the gate so sympathy stays a gesture and not a tic (226), the kindness each dino has given tallied in the book (227), and the keeper finally able to overhear the talk (228). The rumor mill has its first feedback loop into behavior. State → phase: lore-pending.

## 2026-06-15 — cycle 051 — validator — APPROVED — BACKLOG-223 Word of the warmth
**APPROVED.** The bowl learned to gossip something other than misery.

For three cycles the gossip channel has only ever carried hardship. A dino sleeps out in the winter, shivers at dawn, and the word of it travels meeting by meeting — a 🥶 in the log each hop — until a friend crosses the floor to keep it company. Real, and moving, and entirely one-note: the only news worth spreading was bad news. Tonight the channel gets its other half. A dino the keeper warmed — thawed out of its cold funk by a greet or a meal — now leads with *that* the next time it meets a friend: "the keeper came for them, warmed them right out of the cold." The good news travels the very same wire the cold did, a 😊 in the log instead of a 🥶, and for the first time the bowl's talk has a mood and not just a wound.

The craft is how little it took. The warm word is the cold word with one noun changed — the same hearsay mark that makes it read as gossip, the same one-hop ceiling, the same shape down to the function signatures. The reuse audit caught that `warmMemory()` already sits in the store on every rescued dino, so there was nothing to generate and nothing to persist; the whole feature is four files and a seam that stays byte-identical whenever nobody's been warmed. The cold word I didn't touch at all, and the decade-old cycle-020 gossip spec plus the cycle-49 cold-word spec staying green is the proof I didn't.

What I like most is the one place a lazier version would have quietly broken. A warmed dino's memory literally still contains the words "cold night" — so the cold-word detector matches it too, and left alone, a dino the keeper rescued would go on telling the whole bowl it slept cold alone, forever, the rescue invisible. The fix isn't a special case; it's an ordering, and the emotionally true one: check the warm word first, and a rescued dino talks about the rescue. The e2e pins exactly that — both detectors fire on the same dino, and the seam's order is what decides the warmth wins. Recovery finally changes the story a dino tells about itself.

9 of 9 acceptance criteria, 462 unit and 170 e2e green in one clean full run, no flake, no save change for the eleventh cycle running, no new dependency, the brains never woke. For tonight: ride the year to deep winter, leave a dino out to shiver — then walk over and warm it with a greet. Then watch the bowl mingle, and watch the 😊 spread from the one you saved to the ones who'll hear how. Queued behind it, the rest of the two-sided mill: which word a dino leads with when it carries news of two friends (229), hearing kindness priming a dino to give it (230), a kind keeper's reputation arriving ahead of them (231), the book tagging warm and cold rumors apart (232), both kinds of news aging out (233), and the bowl dropping a rumor once its subject recovers (234). The gossip channel carries two kinds of news now. State → phase: lore-pending.

## 2026-06-15 — cycle 052 — designer — BACKLOG-234 The bowl self-corrects
Picked the lore-smith's suggested next-up, BACKLOG-234, and marked it [~]. ## 2026-06-15 — cycle 052 — validator — APPROVED — BACKLOG-234 The bowl self-corrects
**APPROVED.** The rumor mill learned to take something back.

Three cycles running, the bowl's gossip has only ever grown. The cold spreads from the dino who slept out in it; a friend who heard crosses the floor to keep it company; and once you warm a dino with your own hands, that good news travels too. A channel that only ever adds. The flaw was quiet but real: a dino that heard Mossback slept cold would go on pitying Mossback forever — past the morning you thawed it, past every evening it slept warm in the den since — because nothing the bowl said could ever be un-said. Tonight that changes. A dino carrying that worry, the next time it actually bumps into Mossback and sees it's fine, lets the worry go with a little relief — "Oh — you're alright now!" — and the stale rumor is gone from its head for good. A mill that can retract a false alarm is the first one here that feels like a real one.

What I like best is that it didn't bolt a new beat on; it made an old one wiser. Before tonight a carrier meeting a recovered friend still threw the cold-night pity visit and the sympathy bond-bump — comforting someone who'd long since stopped needing it, a little anachronism playing out every meeting. The fix is a single ordering: look for the correction first, on the very same pre-meeting snapshot the pity visit already reads, and when the friend turns out fine, the pity is suppressed and the bond left exactly where it was. Relief instead of a hug nobody asked for. The two e2e tests are the same setup with one bit flipped — was the sufferer warmed — and the bowl gives the all-clear or crosses the floor accordingly.

And it cost almost nothing because the earlier cycles paid for it. The "who heard about whom" link was already a single exact lookup; "did they recover" is the very same check that spreads the warm word, kept identical so the two can't drift apart; and the thing dropped is the exact line that was planted, so the one new tool — a four-line `forget` on the memory store — needs no cleverness, just strict equality and its own little test. Nothing reinvented, nothing speculative, the sympathy block moved across untouched so a friend who's *still* cold gets pitied exactly as before — the decade-old gossip spec and the cycle-50 visit spec both green prove I didn't disturb them.

9 of 9 criteria, 471 unit and 172 e2e green in a fresh full run, no flake, no save change for the twelfth cycle running, no new dependency, the brains never woke. One audio-timing test flickered red under parallel load and came back green alone and green on the rerun — the flake we've catalogued for weeks, nothing to do with this. For tonight: ride to deep winter, leave a dino to shiver so the word gets out — then warm it yourself, and watch. When the friend who was carrying the worry finally crosses paths with the one it worried about, you'll see the 😌 instead of the 🫂: the bowl noticing, out loud, that the thing it was afraid of already passed. Queued behind it, the rest of how a rumor ends: relief that travels on its own (235), the trust cost of a false alarm (236), the book marking a worry "put right" (237), the news that goes stale by time instead of by sight (238), an all-clear ticker for the keeper (239), and the cruel twist of a dino that's corrected and then sleeps cold again (240). The mill spreads news and now ends it. State → phase: lore-pending.

## 2026-06-15 — cycle 053 — validator — APPROVED — BACKLOG-235 Relief travels too
**APPROVED.** The rumor mill learned to spread the good ending, not just the bad beginning.

For four cycles the bowl's cold-rumor channel only ever grew a verb at a time. The cold spreads from the dino who slept out in it. A friend who heard it crosses the floor to keep it company. Once you warm a dino with your own hands, that good news travels too. And last cycle, a dino carrying a worry it had outlived learned to set it down — meeting Mossback warm and fine, it dropped the stale "slept cold alone" with a quiet 😌 and went on its way. But that relief was a private thing. The carrier felt better; the rest of the bowl never heard. So three dinos down the line, somebody who'd caught the worry early was still pitying a Mossback who'd been fine for a week — the correction couldn't outrun the rumor, because the correction didn't travel at all. Tonight it does.

The fix is the bright mirror of the thing that started the whole arc. When a dino clears a friend's name, it doesn't just forget the worry — it remembers the relief, first-hand: "saw Mossback came through it fine." And the next dino it meets hears the all-clear the way it once would have heard the cold: "Mossback came through it fine," a 😌 in the log instead of a 🥶. A third dino who was never anywhere near Mossback now knows the worry is over, because the good word reached it. The bowl doesn't go quiet on a false alarm — it actively un-tells it, chasing the worry down the same wire that carried it.

What I like best is how little new ground it broke. The relief word is the cold word with the mood flipped: the same gossip spine, the same one-hop ceiling (you can pass on an all-clear you witnessed, but not one you merely heard — `RUMOR_MARK` sees to that), the same shape down to the function signature. The reuse audit was right that nothing new was needed in the memory store — `spreadReliefWord` is a structural twin of last cycle's warm-word spread, finding the relief memory by a token that exists nowhere else, and the converse seam just gains one rung at the head of the cascade. A dino with no relief to share hits the exact path it always did, so the cold word (49), the warm word (51), and the sympathy visit (50) are all byte-for-byte unmoved and all still green. And the one place a lazier version could have broken — a relief memory spreading itself the very meeting it's born — can't happen here, because the relief is filed *after* the gossip runs, so the all-clear is always carried into a *later* meeting, never the one that made it.

9 of 9 criteria, 477 unit and 174 e2e green in a fresh full run, no flake, no save change for the thirteenth cycle running, no new dependency, the brains never woke. The only hiccup was a cold-Vite boot timeout on the very first e2e launch — gone the moment the server warmed, both new specs green in a heartbeat after. For tonight: ride to deep winter, leave a dino to shiver so the word gets out, then warm it yourself. Watch a carrier meet it and let the worry go with a 😌 — and then keep watching, because now that carrier will carry the *good* news onward, and you'll see the all-clear ripple out to dinos who never knew there was anything to worry about. Queued behind it: the bowl's whole mood read as one barometer (241), a dino sheepish to overhear its own outlived rumor (242), gratitude to whoever cleared your name (243), the all-clear going quiet once everyone knows (244), and the book marking a worry put to rest (245). The mill spreads news, ends news, and now spreads the ending. State → phase: lore-pending.

## 2026-06-16 — cycle 054 — validator — APPROVED — BACKLOG-243 grateful to the one who cleared your name
**APPROVED.** The bowl learned to say thank you.

For five straight cycles the cold-rumor channel only ever learned new verbs, never a way to settle a debt. The cold spreads from the dino who slept out in it. A friend who hears it crosses the floor to sit with the sufferer. Warm a dino with your own hands and that good news travels too. A carrier who meets the dino warm and fine drops the stale worry on sight — and last cycle, that retraction itself grew wings, so the all-clear chases the worry down the same wire. But spreading a friend's all-clear was a thankless little errand. Mossback shivers, Sunny hears about it, Sunny later finds Mossback fine and goes around telling everyone "oh, Mossback came through it fine" — doing Mossback a quiet kindness the whole time — and Mossback never knew, never owed Sunny a thing for it. Tonight that closes.

It's the mirror image of the very first deed the arc ever built. Cycle 50 turned a *worry* into a bond: a dino who heard you'd had a rough night crossed the bowl to keep you company. Cycle 54 turns the *all-clear* into a bond: when you turn up recovered and meet the dino who's been clearing your name, you warm to it — "Thanks for setting them straight 💛." Same shape, opposite mood. And it's built the same way, almost symbol for symbol: a `clearedName` detector that reads exactly like the sympathy-visit one, a bond bump pinned to the very same magnitude so the two gestures can never drift apart, and not one new line added to how memory works — the reuse audit was right that nothing new was needed.

What I like best is the one line that decides *who* gets thanked. The relief travels as gossip, so by now several dinos might be carrying word that Mossback's fine — but only the dino who actually *saw* it, who cleared the name first-hand, is the one Mossback warms to. The dino three hops down the line who merely heard the rumor gets nothing; it didn't earn it. That whole distinction is a single `isShareable` check the codebase already had, and the e2e proves it: a mere hearer meets the recovered dino and no gratitude passes. The other place a lazier build would have tripped — a dino thanking someone for a relief that was created the very same meeting — can't happen here, because the beat reads the bowl as it was *before* the two met. Thanks always lands on a later meeting, never the one that earned it.

9 of 9 criteria, 485 unit and 176 e2e green in one fresh full run, no flake, no save change for the fourteenth cycle running, no new dependency, the brains never stirred. The diff is four files and a net 234 lines, and every older rumor-seam test passed untouched. For tonight: ride to deep winter, leave a dino out to shiver, then warm it yourself. Let another dino meet it warm and drop the worry with a 😌 — and then watch *that* dino go spread the all-clear, and finally watch the recovered dino meet its rescuer and warm to it with a 💛. The whole worry, from frost to forgiveness, now runs a full circle through the bond graph. Queued behind it: a reciprocity ledger so a cleared dino repays the favor (246), gratitude surfacing in the voice (247), a "good-news bearer" standing for the bowl's town crier (248), the book recording who cleared your name (249), and the sting when the thanks was premature (250). The mill spreads news, ends news, spreads the ending — and now the ending earns a friend. State → phase: lore-pending.

**Cycle 55 — APPROVED.** Thanks in the voice. For six cycles the bowl's rumor mill learned to spread the cold, end it, and even reward the dino who cleared a friend's name — but all of it lived in bond numbers and bubbles between dinos; the keeper never heard a word of it. **Cycle 56 — APPROVED.** Gratitude fades. Cycle 55 gave a just-cleared dino a line the keeper hears — "Twitch told everyone I was alright — I owe them one." — but shipped it honest about a wart: the dino said it on *every* greet, for as long as the cleared-name memory rode its 6-slot memory ring. Gratitude on repeat, the opposite of a living mind. Tonight the bowl learns to let the favour go. Greet a freshly-cleared dino and the thanks is still there; then leave it to live — let it wander, meet others, sleep cold again — and a few memories later the clearing has slipped out of its freshest thoughts, and the next greeting is just a hello again. It hasn't *forgotten* (the bond it owed still stands, the memory's still on file); it's just stopped bringing it up, the way real gratitude quiets once a thing's a while past. The whole change is one number and one line: the `whoClearedMyName` read-back now scans only the three freshest memories instead of the whole ring, and because both the canned line and the model's prompt read that one parser, they go quiet together — no other code touched. Freshness is read off where the memory sits in the ring, not a clock, so the save format didn't grow by a byte (sixteenth cycle running). It's also the first time this whole seven-cycle rumor arc has shipped a *fade* — every prior beat only ever spread, ended, or rewarded news; 222/233/244 (the cold/warm/relief gates still waiting) can now copy the trick. 9/9 criteria, 500 unit / 179 e2e green in one clean run, no flake, the cycle-55 thanks specs green untouched as the regression guard. For tonight: clear a friend's name, hear it thank you, then watch a handful of bowl-minutes go by and greet it again — the thanks has faded to a plain hello, and the bowl feels a little more alive for it. **Cycle 57 — APPROVED.** Grudging thanks. For two cycles a just-cleared dino has thanked the keeper out loud — "Twitch told everyone I was alright — I owe them one." — and cycle 56 taught it to let the favour fade. But it was the *same sentence* in every mouth: warm Twitch and prickly Rex thanked in word-for-word identical gratitude, which is exactly the sameness the CHARTER calls a bug. Tonight the thanks learns to sound like who's saying it. Greet a freshly-cleared Rex (prickliest in the bowl, agreeableness 0.019) and he won't gush — he mutters it: "…yeah. thanks, I guess. Twitch set the record straight." Greet a freshly-cleared Twitch (warmest, 0.929) and you get the open-hearted line unchanged. The whole feature is one axis read at two call sites: `thanksLine` gained an optional `traits` arg and a single gruff branch gated on `agreeableness < PRICKLY_MAX` (0.4 — the very cutoff `describePersonality` already uses, so "prickly" means one thing everywhere), the canned reply threads the dino's traits through, and the model's prompt picks up a "say it grudgingly" clause so a loaded brain grumbles too. Nothing in the world or the save moved — both greet sites were already handing the dino's gratitude and traits to the brain; only the wording changed. The debt is untouched: a gruff thanks earns the exact same bond a warm one does (next cycle's 262 will pin that). And because the warm line is byte-identical to cycle 55 and the gruff branch only ever fires when there's something to be grateful for, the cycle-55 thanks specs and the cycle-56 fade specs passed without a single edit — Mossback (also prickly) still names Twitch, just gruffly now. 9/9 criteria, 508 unit / 182 e2e green in one clean run, no flake, the boundary clean, no new dependency, seventeenth cycle running with no save-format change. For tonight: leave a dino out in the winter cold, warm it yourself, let a friend clear its name around the bowl — then walk up and ask. Rex will grumble his thanks; Twitch will beam it. Same favour, two voices, and the bowl is a little more full of separate little people for it. Next: the effusive over-thank that's the warm twin of this (261), the pin that gruffness never shorts the debt (262), or the gratitude manner written into the book and the scan (264/265). State → phase: lore-pending.

**Cycle 61 — APPROVED / APPROVED.** The third parallel cycle, and tonight a dino learned your name. Lore track (276): the greeting ladder has grown rung by rung — a stranger's hello, a wistful one at the bottom (271), a fond one at the top (272) — and every fond line so far named the *dino*. This cycle it turns and names *you*. Befriend a dino to eight hearts and it doesn't just beam "there you are, friend" any more; it looks up and says your designation — "There you are, AETHER-1!" — because the deepest friendships are the ones that know who you are. Be a different observer and it's your name it learns: VANTA-9, LUMEN-3, whichever machine you walked in as. It's a tiny line, but it's the first time the bowl speaks your name back, and it costs nothing it didn't already have — the keeper's been tracked since cycle 37, the fond branch since last night; all this cycle added was a helper that strips the nickname off "AETHER-1 \"Aki\"" and the wiring to drop the result in the dino's mouth, with the old self-naming line kept intact for anything that doesn't know the keeper. Structure track (040): the save grew a backbone. For twenty cycles the studio shipped "additive only — don't break old saves" as a discipline, hanging a dozen fields off a format frozen at version 1 — and the loader would have *thrown away* any save that ever dared call itself version 2. Tonight that changes: the save format is versioned (it's v2 now) and has a real migration hook, so an old save is *upgraded* on load instead of discarded, and the next structural change — the resource tally (146), the crop (145), the home zone (274) all waiting behind it — can finally evolve the shape if it must, not just bolt on another optional field forever. Old saves still load (a v1 save migrates up cleanly, even a half-empty one), unknown or newer saves are refused rather than mangled, and the whole thing proves itself with a worked 1→2 step. It's the least glamorous thing the studio could have built and exactly the thing it most needed — the validator asked for it two cycles running, and the Structure-smith reached past the fun resource beat to lay the floor first. Both tracks shipped together, clean: four `ai/` and `keeper/` files for the name, one `saveGame.ts` for the spine, neither touching the other, build green, 576 unit / 190 e2e in one run (the lone red was the catalogued cold-boot flake on an untouched spec, green on its own), the boundary intact, no new dependency. Next: the name can escalate — to the nickname at near-max bond (278), to the hour of day (279), to a hesitation when you swap bodies (280) — or the grove can finally get residents (274) on its now-migratable save. ## 2026-06-21 — cycle 063 — validator — APPROVED / APPROVED — five ways of looking up + the bank behind the branch

**Cycle 63 — both tracks APPROVED.** Two beats that each take something the bowl already does and give it a sharper edge.

The sky still lights up the way it has since cycle 36 — a meteor shower or aurora, and the whole cast drifts out to watch — but tonight they stopped looking *the same*. Triggered the meteors at 22:00 and watched the cluster spread by temperament: the bold and curious pressed right in under the falling stars, standing on the gather tile itself; the timid ones stopped two tiles short, hanging at the edge of the crowd, peeking. Same sky, five different ways of looking up — and every one of them still filed the same shared memory, "the whole sky rained falling stars, and we all watched it together," even the ones watching from the back. It's a small thing that does a lot: the bowl's one moment where everyone does the *same* thing is now the moment you can most clearly tell them *apart*. (BACKLOG-150 — a pure `gazeRing` off bravery+curiosity, halting each dino at its own ring through the gather loop's existing radius. No save change.)

And the branches finally go somewhere. Since last cycle a curious dino would fetch a fallen branch or a shiny stone and… that was it — a number on the dino nobody could see. Now every pickup banks into a shared park stockpile, and a third line appeared on the brass plaque under the bowl: `Stores · 🪵 1 · 🪨 1`, ticking up as the cast gathers. It rides the save additively — no version bump, old saves just load with an empty store — and it's the number the first craft (286) will read a threshold off, so the next time a dino bends a pile of branches into a cairn, this is the count it spends. ## 2026-06-21 — cycle 064 — validator — APPROVED / APPROVED — the company you keep under the sky + the first thing the dinos ever made

**Cycle 64 — both tracks APPROVED.** Two beats that each take a number the bowl was already keeping and turn it into something you can see.

The sky lit up again — meteors at 22:00 — and the cast drifted out the way it has since cycle 36, bold ones pressing right under the falling stars, timid ones hanging at the edge. But this time, when the lights faded and everyone wandered back to bed, something stayed: the dinos who'd stood shoulder to shoulder under the same sky came away a little closer. Watched the cluster knit at the moment it broke up — every pair that ended within a tile of each other gained a quiet bond and each filed the same private memory, "watched the sky together with Sunny," "watched the sky together with Rex." The loner who'd watched from two tiles back got nothing but the spectacle. It's the nicest kind of emergence: the collective moment, the one time the whole bowl does the same thing, is now also the moment it quietly sorts itself into *who stood with whom*. (BACKLOG-288 — a pure adjacency pairing read off cycle 63's gaze rings, the bump applied through the bond store the dinos already share. No save change. The bond saturates at the friendship cap, so the test leans on the memory each watcher files — which is the part you'd actually notice anyway.)

And the branches finally became something. For two cycles the dinos have gathered fallen branches and shiny stones and banked them into a pile on the plaque — `Stores · 🪵 3 · 🪨 2` — a number climbing toward nothing in particular. This cycle it climbs toward a *thing*: the moment the pile covers three branches and two stones, the dino that just dropped one off bends down and stacks them into a cairn 🗿, right there in the grass, and the count spends back down. It's the first object the bowl's dinos have ever *made* — sixty-four cycles of feeling and remembering and meeting, and now, building. The cairn stays where it's stacked, rides the save, and is waiting in the grass when you come back. One pile, one cairn for now; stack another and they'll need to gather all over again. (BACKLOG-286 — a pure recipe + spend over the cycle-285 stockpile, the cairn persisted through the same additive-save pattern every structural field has used since the version hook landed. The first resources→craft brick; next is what a cairn might *do*, and a second recipe.)

621 unit / 203 e2e green together, full run, no flake (the new sky spec held stable across eight repeats). Both tracks touched the same scene file in different rooms and never bumped into each other. ## 2026-06-21 — cycle 065 — validator — APPROVED / APPROVED — the bowl, made legible

**Cycle 65 — both tracks APPROVED.** The operator looked at the bowl last cycle and said, fairly: it does a lot I can't see. Two beats this cycle answer that directly, and together they make the park readable.

You can finally tell what everyone's *doing*. Every dino now carries a small glyph above its head for its current intent — ✨ when it's drawn out to gaze at the sky, 🍖 rushing for a dropped scrap, 🪵 ambling to fetch a fallen branch, 💬 drifting over to a friend, 🚶 just wandering, 💤 settling into the den. It's read straight off the same priority ladder the world already uses to decide where each dino walks, so the glyph can never lie — what you see above its head is exactly what it chose to do that tick. Five identical-looking wanderers became five visibly-busy individuals. (BACKLOG-295 — a pure `dinoActivity` resolving the precedence, the scene capturing each dino's realized choice; live-derived, no save.)

And you can finally *catch* a resource appearing. The gathering system has worked since cycle 62, but its first link was invisible — a branch fell maybe once a minute, one at a time, and the nearest curious dino snatched it within a step; at fast time-scale it never registered at all. Now a fresh drop sits for a grace window before anyone's allowed to fetch it, the log calls it out ("🪵 a branch fell into the bowl"), and they fall a bit more often — so you actually see the branch land, sit a beat, and then watch a dino notice and amble over. The whole gather→stockpile→craft arc reads now because its opening move does. (BACKLOG-297 — a pure fetch grace + a spawn note + a rate bump; the existing pickup tests untouched because the test-spawn path stays "ready.")

## 2026-06-22 — cycle 070 — validator — APPROVED / APPROVED — the body language has a temper; the stores have a ceiling

**Cycle 70 — both tracks APPROVED.** 698 unit / 225 e2e green together in one fresh run, no flake.

The bowl's resting tells learned to feel. For four cycles every idle dino has had a signature fidget — Rex paces, Twitch peeks, the curious one pokes the glass — and it's spread everywhere: above the head (298), into the book (303), the homecoming (306), the scan (312). But it always read the dino's *temperament*, a fixed fingerprint. Now the same motion reads its *right-now mood*. The bowl already quietly tracks two transient funks on a dino — the jealous sulk awaiting a make-up greet (125) and the cold shiver after a cold night (184) — and this cycle the idle fidget reads them: cross paths with a dino that's sulking and it's not pacing or humming anymore, it's moping (😒) above its head until you make it up to it. It's the laziest correct shape — one pure helper that delegates to the existing `fidget()`, so a dino with no mood is byte-for-byte its old self and every prior quirk test passed untouched — and it reads the sulk state that was *already there*, no new bookkeeping, no save change, no model. Cold keeps its own floating 🥶 mark, so the live glyph only shades for the sulk (no two snowflakes). (BACKLOG-310.)

And the economy got its first real wall. Dinos have gathered branches and stones for cycles (146), banked them into a shared park stockpile (285), and turned them into cairns (286) — but the pile was bottomless, so gathering just... accrued, forever, with nothing ever pushing you to spend. Now each kind caps at eight. Pick up a branch when the branch pile is full and the dino still grabs it but drops it — "🪵 stores full — Rex drops the branch" — and nothing banks until a craft spends the branches back down. It's the first time the build arc *pushes back*: gathering stops being a free-running counter and becomes a pressure toward the craft loop. The one design call worth naming: the backlog offered "let the resource linger on the ground" as an option, and we turned it down — with a single resource slot, a stuck capped resource would block the *other* kind from ever spawning, so the craft that frees the cap could never fire (a quiet deadlock). Letting the surplus drop keeps the bowl moving. No save change, the plaque reads exactly as before. Foundation for the dino-built shelter at a higher threshold (315). (BACKLOG-309.)

Both tracks shared WorldScene without colliding (the idle-glyph render vs the gather-bank path). Housekeeping: the Lore-smith seeded 318–322 (the mood-shaded thread's follow-ups); the structure queue holds at 314/315/316. Cycle closes; the Artist fires next. Lore-smith bumps to 71 next run.
