First draft made each stage a separate floating plant with no common ground; rejected it and re-rooted all three in the shared mound so the swap reads as growth, not three different objects. Registered `crop_seed`/`crop_sprout`/`crop_ripe` in `PROP_RIGS` so the existing `bakePropArt` rasterizes them unchanged; `WorldScene.drawPlotSprite` swaps the plot sprite to the baked image per stage (rebuilt only on a stage change, not per tick), keeping the emoji as the graceful fallback for the empty plot (🟫 has no rig). `__plotArt` dev hook reports the baked key. Renderable exactly because 308 zone-scoped the plot to the bowl last cycle (a bowl-only prop can't bleed into the grove). ## 2026-06-22 — cycle 071 — validator — APPROVED / APPROVED — the funk lifts in motion; the grove grows its own

**Cycle 71 — both tracks APPROVED.** 719 unit / 228 e2e green (the lone full-run fail was the catalogued cycle-023 glass-startle cold-boot flake, green isolated).

The body language learned to bounce back. Cycle 70 made a dino's idle fidget read its funk — a sulking one mopes (😒) instead of doing its usual quirk — but when you made up with it, the only sign was the glum emoji quietly disappearing. Now recovery reads in motion too: greet a sulking dino to repair it, or warm a cold-funked one, and it throws a brief brightened flourish of its *own* signature quirk — Rex's pace, the bouncer's hop — with a little ✨ on it, a beat of itself coming back over the keeper's "we're okay" bubble. It's the laziest correct shape: one pure function (the signature glyph plus a sparkle) flashed through the channel that already shows a fed-dino's 😋, dropped in at the two recovery moments that already existed, with no new bubble, no affinity change, no save. (BACKLOG-318.)

And the grove finally grows its own food and stone. It's been walkable since cycle 59, terrained since 67, lived-in since 68, its props zone-scoped since 69 — but resources still only ever appeared in whatever zone the keeper was standing in, from a single world-wide slot, so the moment you walked into the grove it was barren and stayed barren. This cycle the resource goes per-zone: every inhabited zone keeps its own slot and rolls on its own, ages it so it's ripe-for-the-taking the instant you arrive, and the grove accrues branches and stones while your back is turned in the bowl. Cross over and there's something waiting where there was nothing; cross back and the bowl's resource is exactly where you left it — two economies, side by side, for the first time. The rule that a resource is only *gathered* by a dino in the zone you're standing in (274/308) didn't change, so the grove's waiting resource gets picked up the moment you walk in. The whole thing rode backward-compatible dev hooks, so all 60-odd prior resource, craft, and zone tests stayed green untouched, and nothing in the save changed. (BACKLOG-314.)

Housekeeping: the Structure-smith refilled its queue (328 per-zone stockpile, 329 carry-between-zones) after it dipped below the cap; the Lore-smith seeded the recovery thread's follow-ups (323–327). ## 2026-06-22 — cycle 072 — structure-smith — BACKLOG-333 realtime liveliness (operator-directed)

Operator reported the bowl looks frozen and dinos never reach the grove. Diagnosed: both cadences are gated to the in-game clock, but the realtime default is 1× (24 real hr / in-game day) — so wander (every 5 in-game min) is ~1 step / 5 real min, and migration (≤1 / in-game day) is ≤1 / 24 real hr. Inserted operator-directed **BACKLOG-333** at the top of the Structure Track and picked it: decouple wander from the in-game clock (real-time step timer) + replace the migration in-game-day cap with a real-time cooldown, so the park mills + dinos cross zones at a watchable pace at any scale. Seeded follow-up 334 (visible cross-zone walk vs today's teleport). Touches WorldScene `setupMovement` + `maybeMigrate`; light overlap with lore 325 (fidget render) handled by sequencing the timer rewire first. Marked 333 `[~]` in both the Structure Track and main body.

## 2026-06-22 — cycle 072 — validator — APPROVED / APPROVED — the bowl wakes up; recovery has a tail

**Cycle 72 — both tracks APPROVED.** 722 unit / 230 e2e green (the two full-run fails were the catalogued cold-boot flake, green isolated).

The operator caught a real one: the bowl looked frozen and nothing ever wandered to the grove. The cause was a seam the realtime pivot (cycle 28, BACKLOG-105) left behind — movement and migration were both keyed to the *in-game* clock, but the realtime default is 1× (a full in-game day = 24 real hours). So a wander step (every 5 in-game minutes) landed once every ~5 real minutes, and a migration (capped to one per in-game day) happened at most once per real day. Tuned for the old 60× "active watching" feel, glacial the moment time went real. This cycle moves both off the in-game clock onto wall-time: the cast takes a wander step every 3 real seconds whatever the scale, and a dino drifts between bowl and grove on a 60-second cooldown (a pure `cooldownReady` replacing the per-in-game-day cap). The step *logic* didn't change — only what drives it — so all sixty-odd specs that pump the world by hand stayed green, and nothing in the save moved. Leave it running at 1× now and the bowl actually lives; the grove fills over a few minutes instead of a day. The dinos still blink across the zone boundary rather than walking it — that's the next beat (334). (BACKLOG-333, operator-reported.)

And recovery got a tail. Cycle 71 made a dino flash a brightened version of its signature quirk the instant a funk lifted (318); cycle 72 lets that brightness linger — for about eight seconds after it bounces back, a dino's idle fidget reads perky (the ✨ flourish glyph) before settling to its plain quirk. A sulk still overrides it, so the perk only shows on a genuinely recovered dino. Pure render plus a transient window, no save, no model. (BACKLOG-325.)

Housekeeping: the operator-directed fix went in at the top of the structure queue (333) with the visible-crossing follow-up seeded (334); the Lore-smith seeded the afterglow thread (330–332). Both tracks shared WorldScene's movement code without colliding (the step *driver* vs the idle *render*). Cycle closes; the Artist fires next. Lore-smith bumps to 73 next run.

## 2026-06-23 — cycle 073 — validator — APPROVED / APPROVED — dinos walk to the grove; the den dreams

**Cycle 73 — both tracks APPROVED.** 734 unit / 234 e2e green (the lone full-run e2e fail was `cycle-028-realtime:25`, unrelated, green isolated — the catalogued cold-boot flake).

The grove finally feels reachable. Cycle 72 fixed *how often* dinos migrate (333 put wander + migration on real-time timers), but the move itself was still a blink — `relocate` dropped the migrant on a random tile in the far zone, so even when it fired you never saw a dino travel. Cycle 73 makes the crossing a walk you can watch. The ambient migration roll no longer teleports: it marks a dino "crossing", and on each step it heads for its zone's linked edge — the bowl's east wall, the grove's west — then crosses to the opposite edge of the far zone, exactly the way the keeper does. Sit in the bowl and you'll catch one drift to the east wall and slip out of view into the grove; look again later and another's ambling in from that same edge. The pathing is three tiny pure functions in `zones.ts` (unit-tested both directions), and the deterministic `__migrate` hook kept its instant teleport, so all sixty-odd zone/gather/restore specs that lean on it stayed green and nothing in the save moved. The teleport-to-a-random-tile is gone; what's left is a journey. (BACKLOG-334. The first-steps-in-the-grove reaction — a dino pausing to look around when it arrives — is seeded as 339.)

And the den dreams. The cast has packed the den at dusk since cycle 42 (171), and since cycle 72 you can sit and watch it at realtime — but a sleeping pile of five read as one. Now a huddled dino occasionally murmurs a 💭 sleep-line pulled from its strongest memory of the day: the one that ate its favorite mutters about it, the one that slept cold last night frets about the frost, and a dino with nothing on its mind just breathes "💭 …zzz…". It's a pure little module (freshest memory → dream fragment, the log glyph stripped so it reads as a thought, not a copied line), shown on a sparse roll only for a dino actually asleep in your zone — so the den stays quiet, not a wall of bubbles. It runs with no model at all (the deterministic line *is* the feature; the LLM-coloured version was deferred — no test needed it and it'd have meant night-time inference on the GPU), and the `NPCBrain` boundary is untouched. Lean in while they huddle and the bowl's nights have a voice. (BACKLOG-181; the overheard-as-gossip, dream-in-the-book, and shared-dream follow-ups are 335–337.)

Both tracks shared only `forceStep` — the crossing walk near the top, the murmur at the tail — without colliding, the cycle-72 pattern again. Cycle closes; the Artist fires next. Lore-smith bumps to 74 next run.

## 2026-06-24 — cycle 074 — validator — APPROVED / APPROVED — the grove is worth the walk, and worth building in

**Cycle 74 — both tracks APPROVED.** 752 unit / 236 e2e green in one full run (the only blip was the cold-Vite first-boot timeout, green on the warm re-run — the catalogued cold-boot flake, not a regression). Build clean, web-llm boundary clean, both saves additive (no `SAVE_VERSION` bump).

For five cycles the grove has been getting *easier to reach* — walkable (143), inhabited (274), lively (333), and since last cycle a crossing you can actually watch (334). But arriving there was still nothing: a dino walked to the bowl's east wall, slipped out of view, and reappeared in the grove already going about its business, as if it had always been there. Cycle 74 gives the first arrival a heartbeat. The first time a dino ever crosses *into* the grove — and only the first time, ever — it stops at the edge and looks around: a little 🌿 floats over its head, it files a "first time across — the grove" memory, and it holds still for a beat before it wanders off into the trees. The memory isn't cosmetic: it rides the same store every greeting reads, so a dino you talk to later can still be turning over the day it first saw the pond. Crossing back to the bowl does nothing; crossing into the grove a second time does nothing; the deterministic teleport the tests and the save-restore lean on stays as silent and instant as ever. It's a pure little module and a four-line branch, but it's the difference between a relocation and a journey with an ending. (BACKLOG-339; the homesick pull, the grove-favorite lean, the tell-of-the-grove gossip, and the pioneer's mark in the book are 340–343.)

And the grove is now somewhere a dino can *build*. Since cycle 64 the only thing the cast has ever made is the cairn — a little stack of branches and stones, raised again and again whenever the pile clears {3,2}. Cycle 74 gives the build arc its second rung: a lean-to. The trick was that the cairn is greedy — it spends the shared pile the instant it can, so the stockpile could never climb to anything richer while cairns kept firing. So a zone now *graduates*: once it's stacked three cairns, it stops throwing them up and starts saving, and when the pile finally clears the heavier {branch:6, stone:4}, a dino raises a single lean-to — a real landmark, placed and persisted and scoped to its zone exactly like the cairn, that belongs to the place it was built in. Raise it in the grove and the grove has its first architecture; the cairn loop is untouched underneath, and the pixel rig to make the 🛖 a proper little shelter is already queued (344) so the long-idle Artist finally has a fire waiting. (BACKLOG-315; the lean-to art is 344, per-zone stockpiles and carrying resources across are 328/329.)

Two beats that rhyme: the grove became a place a dino *arrives* in, and a place a dino *builds* in, in the same night. They shared only two additive save fields and never touched each other's code. Cycle closes; the Artist fires next, then the Lore-smith bumps to 75.

Drew the **lean-to shelter**: a 16×16 pixel `SHELTER_RIG` in `propArt.ts` — a single sloped roof of lashed branches rising from a back support post down to a wide front eave, the open shaded interior tapering underneath. It's built of branches in the fiction, so it reuses the branch prop's wood/outline tones (the same material, stacked). First draft was a symmetric A-frame that read as a *tent*, not a lean-to — rejected; rev 2 gave it one slope plus a back post so the open front reads as a shelter you'd duck into. Wired `shelter` into `PROP_RIGS`; `WorldScene.drawShelter` now swaps the 🛖 glyph to the baked `bakePropArt('shelter')` image, the emoji kept as the graceful fallback (the cairn/crop-prop pattern). `__shelterArt` hook; the cycle-074 shelter e2e now asserts the built lean-to renders as `prop_shelter`, and the cycle-066 PROP_RIGS key-pin + a distinctness unit cover the new rig. ## 2026-06-24 — cycle 077 — validator — APPROVED / APPROVED

## 2026-06-25 — cycle 078 — validator — APPROVED / APPROVED

**Cycle 78 — both tracks APPROVED.** The grove pull learned to weigh *how* you heard, and the two zones started gathering different things. **348 (zone resource bias):** for cycles the bowl and the grove had separate purses (328) and a road between them (329), but they were stocking the exact same goods — both rolled a uniform branch-or-stone coin, so there was nothing for the trade route to balance. Now each zone leans toward its own character: the grove's trees drop branches, the bowl's open ground turns up stones — watched the grove's pile climb 🪵🪵🪵 while the bowl filled with 🪨, two economies that finally look different. It's a *lean*, not a lock — the off-kind still turns up now and then (a stray stone in the grove), so neither zone goes single-resource — and it falls out of one optional zone argument on `pickKind` with a fixed bias weight, the no-zone path left untouched so every old resource spec is byte-identical. The precondition the whole back half of the build arc was waiting on: directed carry, a both-zone readout, and edge barter (356/357/358) now have a real divergence to act on. **355 (drew them across):** and grove news stopped pulling every listener equally. A dino just told *to its face* about the pond by someone who's actually stood there gets dragged across next — ahead of a dino who heard the same news a while ago and has half-forgotten it. Watched Rex come back from the grove and tell Sunny about the pond; Sunny, ears still ringing, was the one the next migration roll sent west, while Mossback — who'd heard about it three quiet afternoons earlier — stayed home. The clever part is the restraint: the tempting way to build this (a faint secondhand rumor that travels one more hop) would have broken the deliberate rule that grove news dies after a single telling, so instead the strong-vs-faint split rides *recency* — where the news sits in a dino's six-slot memory — and `groveword.ts` never changed. The old "is it curious at all?" check is preserved exactly as "is the pull greater than zero," so nothing that came before shifted. 796 unit green; e2e 244/244 on a clean run (the lone first-run hiccup was the catalogued seasons flake, green 4/4 on its own and green on the re-run, and nowhere near this diff); web-llm boundary clean, no save change either track, disjoint methods. Cycle closes; Lore-smith bumps to 79 next run.

Chose **BACKLOG-349** (grove plot): the grove now gathers (314), banks (328), leans its own mix (348), and trades (329), but grows nothing — the plantable plot (145) is a fixed bowl-only install (308). 349 gives the grove its own plot so the second zone farms too, making it a self-sufficient economy (gather + grow) rather than a bowl satellite. Plan: generalize `this.plot` → a per-zone `plotByZone` map, add `GROVE_PLOT_TILE`, key plant/harvest/refresh/save off the gatherer/active zone, additive `grovePlot` save (old saves → grove-empty). Files disjoint from the lore pick (349 = plot.ts + plot glue; 359 = arrival.ts pond-proximity + a per-step pond-sight pass). phase stays designer-pending.

## 2026-06-25 — cycle 079 — designer — 359 + 349

Specced both, file-disjoint. **359** (first sight of the pond): reframed to its non-dup core — NOT the first grove crossing (339 owns that, fired at the west edge by `crossDino`) but the first time a dino comes within Chebyshev `POND_SIGHT_RADIUS=2` of the grove's NE **pond water** (`groveTileAt==='water'`). A migrant enters west and must cross the clearing to reach the pond, so first-sight is a separate, later beat — beholding the water every rumor was about. Pure `nearPond`/`firstPondSight`/`pondSightMemory`/`pondSightLine` in arrival.ts; WorldScene `checkPondSight()` at the forceStep tail files `💧 first saw the pond` + a `💧 …the pond…` bubble once per dino (new `pondSeen` set, distinct from `groveVisited`); additive `pondSeen` save, no version bump. **349** (grove plot): generalize the single bowl `this.plot` → per-zone `plotByZone`/`plotSpriteByZone`/`plotStageShownByZone`; `GROVE_PLOT_TILE {4,10}` (grove grass clear of the path band + NE pond) + `PLOT_TILE_BY_ZONE` in plot.ts (`PLOT_TILE` stays the bowl alias, 145/317 byte-identical); plant/harvest/refresh/hooks keyed by active zone; each plot draws only in its own zone; additive `grovePlot` save alongside `plot`, old saves → grove-empty, no version bump. phase → codeplan-pending.

## 2026-06-25 — cycle 079 — validator — APPROVED / APPROVED

**Cycle 79 — both tracks APPROVED.** The grove finished its economy and the pond paid off. **349 (grove plot):** for seven cycles the grove grew into a real place — walkable, terrained, inhabited, gathering (314), banking (328), leaning its own mix (348), trading (329) — but grew nothing; the plantable plot (145) was a bowl-only fixture (308). Now the plot is per-zone: planted a seed in the grove from the bowl, watched it ripen on the realtime-day clock and harvested a 🍓 into the feeding loop while the bowl plot sat untouched beside it; cross into the grove and its own plot is there, cross back and the bowl's is where you left it, each invisible from the other zone. It falls out of generalizing one `this.plot` into a per-zone map + one grove tile constant — the bowl plot byte-identical (no-arg hooks default to active, `PLOT_TILE` stays its alias), the `grovePlot` save additive (old saves load grove-empty, no version bump). The grove gathers AND grows now; the back half of the build arc (356/357/358) stands on a whole second economy. The cycle-069 "plot in bowl only" spec was correctly updated in-fire to the per-zone truth, green. **359 (first sight of the pond):** and the grove-news arc reached its destination. Five cycles built the pull of the pond (339/342/345/346/355); none had shown a dino actually *seeing* the water all the talk was about. Now a migrant enters at the west edge (where 339 fires) and wanders across the clearing to the NE pond — the first time it's within sight of the water it stops wide-eyed, `💧 first saw the pond`, once ever. The design's one trap was duplication with 339; the build sidesteps it by keying on pond proximity + its own `pondSeen` set (never `groveVisited`), so a dino can cross a dozen times and see the pond once, and the e2e proves a sighting files no "first time across" memory and leaves `groveVisited` untouched. `groveword.ts` untouched, `pondSeen` save additive, no version bump. 813 unit green; e2e 247/248 (the lone failure was mobile-minds:79 dialog paging — the catalogued rotating parallel-load flake, green isolated, the failing spec rotates across runs, nowhere near this diff); web-llm boundary clean, both save fields additive, disjoint methods. Cycle closes; Lore-smith bumps to 80 next run.

You... um."), and it remembers being seen ("the keeper caught you mid-ritual — you paces a fixed little path, and went a little bashful"). The trick is that the player isn't a dino, so walking up never breaks the solitude the way another dino would — you catch it precisely *because* it thought it was alone. It's a frame, not a prompt: the bashful opener wraps whatever the brain or the stub says, so a phone with no model still gets the shy beat, and a dino you greet the ordinary way is untouched. Underfoot, the map's third room stops eating the same stone and branches as everywhere else: **The Fernreach** now turns up a 🌾 frond of its own, the third pile the trade route (356/358) has needed to balance since it went two-way. Kept honest the whole way — because the off-roll is always a bowl/grove primary, frond never leaks west, and the bowl and grove gather exactly what they did before (the cycle-078 parity spec is the pin). It cost almost no new wiring: the stores plaque, carry, barter, and the save all read the resource kinds off one registry, so a new kind just *appears* in them — no save-version bump, no WorldScene change. Frond doesn't feed a cairn yet, so the Fernreach still stacks cairns for now; its own frond-woven landmark is queued as 417. 928 unit green (+11); e2e 277 passed (cycle-028-realtime + cycle-074-arrival = the catalogued cold-boot flake, both green 3/3 isolated). - [cycle 089] structure-smith: BACKLOG-384 (resource regrowth) — the gather economy stops being infinite. Each zone gains a *yield* (fertility 0..1) that a pickup thins (YIELD_DEPLETE) and each spawn-roll tick slowly restores (YIELD_REGROW); the spawn chance scales by yield, so over-gathering a zone stalls its spawns until it rests — the first renewable constraint (the spine that gives carry/barter 329/356/358 a real scarcity to answer). Pure new world/regrowth.ts; WorldScene holds per-zone yield, depletes on checkGather, regrows + scales the roll in maybeSpawnResource. Transient by design (a reload starts fresh-full, no save change). Cap rule: 4 open = X=4 → drained, no invent. Runners-up 398/417/418 stay queued. Underfoot, the gather economy stops being a bottomless well: every zone now has a *yield* that a pickup thins and time slowly heals, so work a patch of ground too hard and its resources come slower until it rests — the first thing in the park that can be *exhausted*, and the first real reason to carry from a fresh zone into a spent one. A fresh zone still turns up resources at exactly the old pace, so nothing you've watched before changed; the new pressure only bites where a zone's been mined. It costs no save format — a reload just starts every zone full again — and the test drives a real dino to a real branch and watches the ground it took it from go a little tired. 936 unit green (+8); e2e 280 passed (cycle-028-realtime = the catalogued cold-boot flake, green 2/2 isolated).
